	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Americas</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"><div id="mw-fr-revisiontag" class="flaggedrevs_short flaggedrevs_stable_synced plainlinks noprint"><div class="flaggedrevs_short_basic"><span aria-disabled='false' title='Changes must be reviewed before being displayed on this page.' class='flaggedrevs-icon oo-ui-widget oo-ui-widget-enabled oo-ui-iconElement-icon oo-ui-icon-articleSearch oo-ui-iconElement oo-ui-labelElement-invisible oo-ui-iconWidget'></span><span id='mw-fr-revisiontoggle' aria-disabled='false' title='show/hide details' class='fr-toggle-arrow oo-ui-widget oo-ui-widget-enabled oo-ui-indicatorElement-indicator oo-ui-indicator-down oo-ui-indicatorElement oo-ui-labelElement-invisible oo-ui-indicatorWidget'></span></div>

</p>
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Landmass comprising North America, Central America and South America</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a href="/wiki/File:N%26SAmerica-pol.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/N%26SAmerica-pol.jpg/230px-N%26SAmerica-pol.jpg" decoding="async" width="230" height="346" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/N%26SAmerica-pol.jpg/345px-N%26SAmerica-pol.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/N%26SAmerica-pol.jpg/460px-N%26SAmerica-pol.jpg 2x" data-file-width="970" data-file-height="1460" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:N%26SAmerica-pol.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1990s <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">CIA</a> political map of the Americas in <a href="/wiki/Lambert_azimuthal_equal-area_projection" title="Lambert azimuthal equal-area projection">Lambert azimuthal equal-area projection</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <b>Americas</b> (also collectively called <b>America</b>; <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Amérique</i>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>: <i lang="nl">Amerika</i>, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <i>América</i>) comprise the totality of the <a href="/wiki/Continents" class="mw-redirect" title="Continents">continents</a> of <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Together, they make up most of the land in Earth's <a href="/wiki/Western_hemisphere" class="mw-redirect" title="Western hemisphere">western hemisphere</a> and comprise the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a>.
</p><p>Along with their <a href="/wiki/Lists_of_islands_of_the_Americas" title="Lists of islands of the Americas">associated islands</a>, they cover 8% of <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">Earth</a>'s total surface area and 28.4% of its land area. The topography is dominated by the <a href="/wiki/American_Cordillera" title="American Cordillera">American Cordillera</a>, a long chain of mountains that runs the length of the west coast. The flatter eastern side of the Americas is dominated by large river basins, such as the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_river_basin" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon river basin">Amazon</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._Lawrence_River" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Lawrence River">St. Lawrence River</a> / <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">Great Lakes</a> basin, <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_river_basin" class="mw-redirect" title="Mississippi river basin">Mississippi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/La_Plata_river_basin" class="mw-redirect" title="La Plata river basin">La Plata</a>. Since the Americas extend 14,000&#160;km (8,700&#160;mi) from north to south, the climate and ecology vary widely, from the arctic <a href="/wiki/Tundra" title="Tundra">tundra</a> of <a href="/wiki/Northern_Canada" title="Northern Canada">Northern Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a>, to the <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rain_forest" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical rain forest">tropical rain forests</a> in <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">Central America</a> and South America.
</p><p>Humans first <a href="/wiki/Settlement_of_the_Americas" title="Settlement of the Americas">settled the Americas</a> from <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a> between 42,000 and 17,000 years ago. A second migration of <a href="/wiki/Na-Dene_languages" title="Na-Dene languages">Na-Dene speakers</a> followed later from Asia. The subsequent migration of the <a href="/wiki/Inuit" title="Inuit">Inuit</a> into the <a href="/wiki/Neoarctic" class="mw-redirect" title="Neoarctic">neoarctic</a> around 3500 BCE completed what is generally regarded as the settlement by the <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">indigenous peoples of the Americas</a>.
</p><p>The first known European settlement in the Americas was by the <a href="/wiki/Norsemen" title="Norsemen">Norse</a> explorer <a href="/wiki/Leif_Erikson" title="Leif Erikson">Leif Erikson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> However, the colonization never became permanent and was later abandoned. The Spanish <a href="/wiki/Voyages_of_Christopher_Columbus" title="Voyages of Christopher Columbus">voyages of Christopher Columbus</a> from 1492 to 1502 resulted in permanent contact with European (and subsequently, other <a href="/wiki/Old_World" title="Old World">Old World</a>) powers, which led to the <a href="/wiki/Columbian_exchange" title="Columbian exchange">Columbian exchange</a> and inaugurated a period of <a href="/wiki/Exploration" title="Exploration">exploration</a>, <a href="/wiki/Conquest_(military)" class="mw-redirect" title="Conquest (military)">conquest</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Colonization" title="Colonization">colonization</a> whose effects and consequences persist to the present. The Spanish presence involved the <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_the_Spanish_New_World_colonies" title="Slavery in the Spanish New World colonies">enslavement of large numbers of the indigenous population of America</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> During the first half of the 16th century, Spanish colonists conducted raids throughout the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Basin" title="Caribbean Basin">Caribbean Basin</a>, bringing captives from Central America, northern South America, and <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a> back to <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a> and other Spanish settlements.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Diseases introduced from <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West Africa</a> <a href="/wiki/Population_history_of_indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Population history of indigenous peoples of the Americas">devastated the indigenous peoples</a>, and the European powers <a href="/wiki/European_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="European colonization of the Americas">colonized the Americas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Taylor_2001_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Taylor_2001-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Mass <a href="/wiki/European_emigration" title="European emigration">emigration from Europe</a>, including large numbers of <a href="/wiki/Indentured_servitude" title="Indentured servitude">indentured servants</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">importation of African slaves</a> largely replaced the indigenous peoples.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Decolonization_of_the_Americas" title="Decolonization of the Americas">Decolonization of the Americas</a> began with the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a> in the 1770s and largely ended with the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish–American War">Spanish–American War</a> in the late 1890s. Currently, almost all of the population of the Americas resides in independent countries; however, the legacy of the colonization and settlement by Europeans is that the Americas share many common cultural traits, most notably <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> and the use of <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">Indo-European languages</a>: primarily <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language_in_the_Americas" title="Spanish language in the Americas">Spanish</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_American_English" title="North American English">English</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Portuguese" title="Brazilian Portuguese">Portuguese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canadian_French" title="Canadian French">French</a>, and, to a lesser extent, <a href="/wiki/Surinamese_Dutch" title="Surinamese Dutch">Dutch</a>.
</p><p>The Americas are home to over a billion inhabitants, two-thirds of whom reside in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>. It is home to eight <a href="/wiki/Megacity" title="Megacity">megacities</a> (<a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_area" title="Metropolitan area">metropolitan areas</a> with ten million inhabitants or more): <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_metropolitan_area" class="mw-redirect" title="New York City metropolitan area">New York City</a> (23.9 million), <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City_metropolitan_area" class="mw-redirect" title="Mexico City metropolitan area">Mexico City</a> (21.2 million), <a href="/wiki/Sao_Paulo_Metropolitan_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="Sao Paulo Metropolitan Area">São Paulo</a> (21.2 million), <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_metropolitan_area" title="Los Angeles metropolitan area">Los Angeles</a> (18.8 million), <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires_metropolitan_area" class="mw-redirect" title="Buenos Aires metropolitan area">Buenos Aires</a> (15.6 million),<sup id="cite_ref-indecpop_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indecpop-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro_metropolitan_area" class="mw-redirect" title="Rio de Janeiro metropolitan area">Rio de Janeiro</a> (13.0 million), <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Area_of_Bogot%C3%A1" title="Metropolitan Area of Bogotá">Bogotá</a> (10.4 million), and <a href="/wiki/Lima_metropolitan_area" title="Lima metropolitan area">Lima</a> (10.1 million).
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_and_naming"><span id="Naming">Etymology and naming</span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology and naming">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Naming_of_the_Americas" title="Naming of the Americas">Naming of the Americas</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amerigo_Vespucci_(with_turban).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Amerigo_Vespucci_%28with_turban%29.jpg/200px-Amerigo_Vespucci_%28with_turban%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="271" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Amerigo_Vespucci_%28with_turban%29.jpg/300px-Amerigo_Vespucci_%28with_turban%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Amerigo_Vespucci_%28with_turban%29.jpg/400px-Amerigo_Vespucci_%28with_turban%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="680" data-file-height="923" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amerigo_Vespucci_(with_turban).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>America is named after Italian explorer <a href="/wiki/Amerigo_Vespucci" title="Amerigo Vespucci">Amerigo Vespucci</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>The name America was first recorded in 1507. <a href="/wiki/Christie%27s" title="Christie&#39;s">Christie's</a> auction house says a two-dimensional globe created by <a href="/wiki/Martin_Waldseem%C3%BCller" title="Martin Waldseemüller">Martin Waldseemüller</a> was the earliest recorded use of the term.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> The name was also used (together with the related term <i>Amerigen</i>) in the <i><a href="/wiki/Cosmographiae_Introductio" title="Cosmographiae Introductio">Cosmographiae Introductio</a></i>, apparently written by <a href="/wiki/Matthias_Ringmann" title="Matthias Ringmann">Matthias Ringmann</a>, in reference to South America.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> It was applied to both North and South America by <a href="/wiki/Gerardus_Mercator" title="Gerardus Mercator">Gerardus Mercator</a> in 1538. America derives from <i>Americus</i>, the <a href="/wiki/Latinisation_of_names" title="Latinisation of names">Latin</a> version of Italian explorer <a href="/wiki/Amerigo_Vespucci" title="Amerigo Vespucci">Amerigo Vespucci</a>'s first name. The feminine form <i>America</i> accorded with the feminine names of <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Smiths_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Smiths-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In modern English, North and South America are generally considered separate continents, and taken together are called <i>America</i><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-oxfordc_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oxfordc-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> or <i>the Americas</i> in the plural. When conceived as a unitary continent, the form is generally <i>the continent of America</i> in the singular. However, without a clarifying context, singular <i>America</i> in English commonly refers to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_of_America" class="mw-redirect" title="United States of America">United States of America</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-oxfordc_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oxfordc-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Historically, in the English-speaking world, the term America used to refer to a single continent until the 1950s (as in <a href="/wiki/Hendrik_Willem_van_Loon" title="Hendrik Willem van Loon">Van Loon</a>'s <i>Geography</i> of 1937): According to historians Kären Wigen and Martin W. Lewis,<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886047036">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>While it might seem surprising to find North and South America still joined into a single continent in a book published in the United States in 1937, such a notion remained fairly common until World War II.  It cannot be coincidental that this idea served American geopolitical designs at the time, which sought both Western Hemispheric domination and disengagement from the "Old World" continents of Europe, Asia, and Africa. By the 1950s, however, virtually all American geographers had come to insist that the visually distinct landmasses of North and South America deserved separate designations.
</p></blockquote>
<p>This shift did not seem to happen in most other <a href="/wiki/Cultural_area" title="Cultural area">cultural spheres</a> on Earth, such as Romance-speaking (including France, Belgium, Luxembourg, Italy, Portugal, Spain, Romania, Switzerland, and the Romance-speaking countries of <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a> and <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>), Germanic (but excluding English) speaking (including Germany, Austria, Switzerland, Belgium, The Netherlands, Luxembourg, Denmark, Norway, Sweden, Icelands, Faroe Islands), Baltic-Slavic languages (including Czech Rep., Slovakia, Poland, Ukraine, Belarus, Lithunia, Latvia, Estonia, Russia, Slovenia, Croatia, Bosnia-Herzegovina, Serbia, Montenegro, Bulgaria) and in many other spheres, where America is still considered a continent encompassing the <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a> <a href="/wiki/Subcontinent" class="mw-redirect" title="Subcontinent">subcontinents</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> as well as <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">Central America</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Americas" title="History of the Americas">History of the Americas</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Settlement">Settlement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Settlement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information&#32;on theories of Paleo-Indian migration: <a href="/wiki/Settlement_of_the_Americas" title="Settlement of the Americas">Settlement of the Americas</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Spreading_homo_sapiens_la.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Spreading_homo_sapiens_la.svg/300px-Spreading_homo_sapiens_la.svg.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Spreading_homo_sapiens_la.svg/450px-Spreading_homo_sapiens_la.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Spreading_homo_sapiens_la.svg/600px-Spreading_homo_sapiens_la.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="851" data-file-height="400" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Spreading_homo_sapiens_la.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of <a href="/wiki/Early_human_migrations" title="Early human migrations">early human migrations</a> based on the <a href="/wiki/Recent_African_origin_of_modern_humans" title="Recent African origin of modern humans">Out of Africa theory</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Paleo-Indians" title="Paleo-Indians">The first inhabitants</a> migrated into the Americas from Asia. Habitation sites are known in <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Yukon" title="Yukon">Yukon</a> from at least 20,000 years ago, with suggested ages of up to 40,000 years.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kind_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kind-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
Beyond that, the specifics of the <a href="/wiki/Paleo-Indian" class="mw-redirect" title="Paleo-Indian">Paleo-Indian</a> migration to and throughout the Americas, including the dates and routes traveled, are subject to ongoing research and discussion.<sup id="cite_ref-national_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-national-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Widespread habitation of the Americas occurred during the <a href="/wiki/Late_Glacial_Maximum#North_America" class="mw-redirect" title="Late Glacial Maximum">late glacial maximum</a>, from 16,000 to 13,000 years ago.<sup id="cite_ref-kind_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kind-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Palazzo_Ferreria_statue_4_America.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Palazzo_Ferreria_statue_4_America.jpeg/220px-Palazzo_Ferreria_statue_4_America.jpeg" decoding="async" width="220" height="295" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Palazzo_Ferreria_statue_4_America.jpeg/330px-Palazzo_Ferreria_statue_4_America.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Palazzo_Ferreria_statue_4_America.jpeg/440px-Palazzo_Ferreria_statue_4_America.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1936" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Palazzo_Ferreria_statue_4_America.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Statue representing the Americas at <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_Ferreria" title="Palazzo Ferreria">Palazzo Ferreria</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Valletta" title="Valletta">Valletta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a></div></div></div>
<p>The traditional theory has been that these early migrants moved into the <a href="/wiki/Beringia" title="Beringia">Beringia</a> land bridge between eastern Siberia and present-day Alaska around 40,000–17,000 years ago,<sup id="cite_ref-SpencerWells2_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SpencerWells2-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> when sea levels were significantly lowered during the <a href="/wiki/Quaternary_glaciation" title="Quaternary glaciation">Quaternary glaciation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-national_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-national-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Smithsonian_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Smithsonian-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> These people are believed to have followed herds of now-extinct <a href="/wiki/Pleistocene_megafauna" title="Pleistocene megafauna">pleistocene megafauna</a> along <i>ice-free corridors</i> that stretched between the <a href="/wiki/Laurentide_Ice_Sheet" title="Laurentide Ice Sheet">Laurentide</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cordilleran_Ice_Sheet" title="Cordilleran Ice Sheet">Cordilleran</a> ice sheets.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Another route proposed is that, either on foot or using <a href="/wiki/Boat#History" title="Boat">primitive boats</a>, they migrated down the Pacific coast to South America.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Evidence of the latter would since have been covered by a <a href="/wiki/Sea_level_rise" title="Sea level rise">sea level rise</a> of hundreds of meters following the last ice age.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Both routes may have been taken, although the genetic evidences suggests a single founding population.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Microsatellite_(genetics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Microsatellite (genetics)">micro-satellite</a> diversity and distributions specific to <a href="/wiki/South_American_Indigenous_people" class="mw-redirect" title="South American Indigenous people">South American Indigenous people</a> indicates that certain populations have been isolated since the initial colonization of the region.<sup id="cite_ref-subclades_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-subclades-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A second migration occurred after the initial peopling of the Americas;<sup id="cite_ref-Meltzer2009_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Meltzer2009-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Na-Dene_languages" title="Na-Dene languages">Na Dene speakers</a> found predominantly in North American groups at varying genetic rates with the highest frequency found among the <a href="/wiki/Athabaskan_languages" title="Athabaskan languages">Athabaskans</a> at 42% derive from this second wave.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Linguists" class="mw-redirect" title="Linguists">Linguists</a> and <a href="/wiki/Biologist" title="Biologist">biologists</a> have reached a similar conclusion based on analysis of <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_languages_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous languages of the Americas">Amerindian language groups</a> and <a href="/wiki/ABO_blood_group_system" title="ABO blood group system">ABO blood group system</a> distributions.<sup id="cite_ref-Meltzer2009_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Meltzer2009-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Then the people of the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_small_tool_tradition" title="Arctic small tool tradition">Arctic small tool tradition</a> a broad cultural entity that developed along the <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Peninsula" title="Alaska Peninsula">Alaska Peninsula</a>, around <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Bay" title="Bristol Bay">Bristol Bay</a>, and on the eastern shores of the Bering Strait around 2,500&#160;BCE (4,500&#160;years ago) moved into North America.<sup id="cite_ref-Fagan_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fagan-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> The Arctic small tool tradition, a <a href="/wiki/Paleo-Eskimo" title="Paleo-Eskimo">Paleo-Eskimo</a> culture branched off into two cultural variants, including the <a href="/wiki/Pre-Dorset" title="Pre-Dorset">Pre-Dorset</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Independence_II_culture" title="Independence II culture">Independence traditions</a> of Greenland.<sup id="cite_ref-YoungBjerregaard2008_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YoungBjerregaard2008-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The descendants of the Pre-Dorset cultural group, the <a href="/wiki/Dorset_culture" title="Dorset culture">Dorset culture</a> was displaced by the final migrants from the Bering sea coast line the ancestors of modern <a href="/wiki/Inuit" title="Inuit">Inuit</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Thule_people" title="Thule people">Thule people</a> by 1000&#160;<a href="/wiki/Common_Era" title="Common Era">Common Era</a> (CE).<sup id="cite_ref-YoungBjerregaard2008_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YoungBjerregaard2008-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Around the same time as the Inuit migrated into Greenland, <a href="/wiki/Norse_colonization_of_the_Americas" class="mw-redirect" title="Norse colonization of the Americas">Viking settlers</a> began arriving in <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a> in 982 and <a href="/wiki/Vinland" title="Vinland">Vinland</a> shortly thereafter, establishing a settlement at <a href="/wiki/L%27Anse_aux_Meadows" title="L&#39;Anse aux Meadows">L'Anse aux Meadows</a>, near the northernmost tip of <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_(island)" title="Newfoundland (island)">Newfoundland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> The Viking settlers quickly abandoned Vinland, and disappeared from Greenland by 1500.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-Columbian_era">Pre-Columbian era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Pre-Columbian era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pre-Columbian_era" title="Pre-Columbian era">Pre-Columbian era</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Parkin_Mounds_Aerial_HRoe_2016.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Parkin_Mounds_Aerial_HRoe_2016.jpg/220px-Parkin_Mounds_Aerial_HRoe_2016.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Parkin_Mounds_Aerial_HRoe_2016.jpg/330px-Parkin_Mounds_Aerial_HRoe_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/39/Parkin_Mounds_Aerial_HRoe_2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="267" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Parkin_Mounds_Aerial_HRoe_2016.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Parkin_Archeological_State_Park" title="Parkin Archeological State Park">Parkin Site</a>, a Mississippian site in Arkansas, circa 1539</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Pre-Columbian_era" title="Pre-Columbian era">pre-Columbian era</a> incorporates all <a href="/wiki/Archaeology_of_the_Americas" title="Archaeology of the Americas">period subdivisions</a> in the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Americas" title="History of the Americas">history and prehistory of the Americas</a> before the appearance of significant European influences on the American continents, spanning the time of the <a href="/wiki/Migration_to_the_New_World" class="mw-redirect" title="Migration to the New World">original settlement</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Upper_Paleolithic" title="Upper Paleolithic">Upper Paleolithic</a> to <a href="/wiki/European_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="European colonization of the Americas">European colonization</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Early_Modern_period" class="mw-redirect" title="Early Modern period">Early Modern period</a>. The term <i>Pre-Columbian</i> is used especially often in the context of the great <a href="/wiki/List_of_pre-Columbian_civilizations" class="mw-redirect" title="List of pre-Columbian civilizations">indigenous civilizations of the Americas</a>, such as those of <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerica" title="Mesoamerica">Mesoamerica</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Olmec" class="mw-redirect" title="Olmec">Olmec</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Toltec" title="Toltec">Toltec</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Teotihuacano" class="mw-redirect" title="Teotihuacano">Teotihuacano</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Zapotec_civilization" title="Zapotec civilization">Zapotec</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Mixtec_civilization" class="mw-redirect" title="Mixtec civilization">Mixtec</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Aztec" class="mw-redirect" title="Aztec">Aztec</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Maya_civilization" title="Maya civilization">Maya</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Andes</a> (<a href="/wiki/Tahuantinsuyu" class="mw-redirect" title="Tahuantinsuyu">Inca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moche_(culture)" class="mw-redirect" title="Moche (culture)">Moche</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muisca_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Muisca people">Muisca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ca%C3%B1ari" title="Cañari">Cañaris</a>).
</p><p>Many pre-Columbian <a href="/wiki/Civilization" title="Civilization">civilizations</a> established characteristics and hallmarks which included permanent or urban settlements, agriculture, civic and monumental architecture, and <a href="/wiki/Complex_society" title="Complex society">complex societal hierarchies</a>. Some of these civilizations had long faded by the time of the first permanent European arrivals (c. late 15th–early 16th centuries), and are known only through <a href="/wiki/Archaeology" title="Archaeology">archeological</a> investigations. Others were contemporary with this period, and are also known from historical accounts of the time. A few, such as the Maya, had their own written records. However, most Europeans of the time viewed such texts as pagan, and much was destroyed in Christian pyres. Only a few hidden documents remain today, leaving modern historians with glimpses of ancient culture and knowledge.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_colonization">European colonization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: European colonization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/European_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="European colonization of the Americas">European colonization of the Americas</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Landing_of_Columbus_(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Landing_of_Columbus_%282%29.jpg/220px-Landing_of_Columbus_%282%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Landing_of_Columbus_%282%29.jpg/330px-Landing_of_Columbus_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Landing_of_Columbus_%282%29.jpg/440px-Landing_of_Columbus_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1971" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Landing_of_Columbus_(2).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> leads expedition to the New World, 1492.</div></div></div>
<p>Although there had been previous <a href="/wiki/Pre-Columbian_trans-oceanic_contact_theories" title="Pre-Columbian trans-oceanic contact theories">trans-oceanic contact</a>, large-scale European colonization of the Americas began with the first voyage of <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> in 1492. The first Spanish settlement in the Americas was <a href="/wiki/La_Isabela" title="La Isabela">La Isabela</a> in northern <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a>. This town was abandoned shortly after in favor of <a href="/wiki/Santo_Domingo" title="Santo Domingo">Santo Domingo de Guzmán</a>, founded in 1496, the oldest American city of European foundation. This was the base from which the Spanish monarchy administered its new colonies and their expansion. Santo Domingo was subject to frequent raids by English and French <a href="/wiki/Piracy_in_the_Caribbean" title="Piracy in the Caribbean">pirates</a>. On the continent, <a href="/wiki/Panama_City" title="Panama City">Panama City</a> on the Pacific coast of Central America, founded on August 15, 1519, played an important role, being the base for the Spanish conquest of South America. The spread of new diseases brought by Europeans and Africans killed many of the inhabitants of North America and South America,<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> with a general <a href="/wiki/Population_history_of_American_indigenous_peoples" class="mw-redirect" title="Population history of American indigenous peoples">population crash of Native Americans</a> occurring in the mid-16th century, often well ahead of European contact.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> European immigrants were often part of state-sponsored attempts to found colonies in the Americas. Migration continued as people moved to the Americas fleeing <a href="/wiki/Religious_persecution" title="Religious persecution">religious persecution</a> or seeking economic opportunities. Millions of individuals were forcibly transported to the Americas as <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slaves</a>, prisoners or <a href="/wiki/Indentured_servitude" title="Indentured servitude">indentured servants</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Americas_independence_map.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Americas_independence_map.PNG/220px-Americas_independence_map.PNG" decoding="async" width="220" height="324" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Americas_independence_map.PNG/330px-Americas_independence_map.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Americas_independence_map.PNG/440px-Americas_independence_map.PNG 2x" data-file-width="862" data-file-height="1270" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Americas_independence_map.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map showing the dates of independence from European powers. Black signifies areas that are <a href="/wiki/Dependent_territory" title="Dependent territory">dependent territories</a> or parts of countries with a capital outside the Americas.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Decolonization_of_the_Americas" title="Decolonization of the Americas">Decolonization of the Americas</a> began with the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Revolution" title="Haitian Revolution">Haitian Revolution</a> in the late 1700s. This was followed by numerous <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_wars_of_independence" title="Latin American wars of independence">Latin American wars of independence</a> in the early 1800s. Between 1811 and 1825, <a href="/wiki/Paraguay" title="Paraguay">Paraguay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gran_Colombia" title="Gran Colombia">Gran Colombia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Provinces_of_Central_America" class="mw-redirect" title="United Provinces of Central America">United Provinces of Central America</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a> gained independence from Spain and Portugal in armed revolutions. After the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_War_of_Independence" title="Dominican War of Independence">Dominican Republic won independence from Haiti</a>, it was re-annexed by Spain in 1861, but reclaimed its independence in 1865 at the conclusion of the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Restoration_War" title="Dominican Restoration War">Dominican Restoration War</a>. The last violent episode of decolonization was the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_War_of_Independence" title="Cuban War of Independence">Cuban War of Independence</a> which became the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish–American War">Spanish–American War</a>, which resulted in the independence of <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> in 1898, and the transfer of sovereignty over <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> from Spain to the United States.
</p><p>Peaceful decolonization began with the purchase by the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> of <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Purchase" title="Louisiana Purchase">Louisiana from France</a> in 1803, <a href="/wiki/Adams%E2%80%93On%C3%ADs_Treaty" title="Adams–Onís Treaty">Florida from Spain</a> in 1819, of <a href="/wiki/Alaska_purchase" class="mw-redirect" title="Alaska purchase">Alaska from Russia</a> in 1867, and the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_the_Danish_West_Indies" title="Treaty of the Danish West Indies">Danish West Indies from Denmark</a> in 1916. <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> became independent of the United Kingdom, starting with the <a href="/wiki/Balfour_Declaration_of_1926" title="Balfour Declaration of 1926">Balfour Declaration of 1926</a>, <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Westminster_1931" title="Statute of Westminster 1931">Statute of Westminster 1931</a>, and ending with the <a href="/wiki/Patriation_of_the_Canadian_Constitution" class="mw-redirect" title="Patriation of the Canadian Constitution">patriation of the Canadian Constitution</a> in 1982. The <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_Newfoundland" title="Dominion of Newfoundland">Dominion of Newfoundland</a> similarly achieved partial independence under the Balfour Declaration and Statute of Westminster, but was re-absorbed into the United Kingdom in 1934. It was subsequently <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_Act" title="Newfoundland Act">confederated with Canada</a> in 1949.
</p><p>The remaining European colonies in the Caribbean began to achieve peaceful independence well after <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a> became independent in 1962, and <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a> both achieved independence in 1966. In the 1970s, the <a href="/wiki/Bahamas" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahamas">Bahamas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grenada" title="Grenada">Grenada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">Dominica</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._Lucia" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Lucia">St. Lucia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/St._Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Vincent and the Grenadines">St. Vincent and the Grenadines</a> all became independent of the United Kingdom, and <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a> became independent of the Netherlands. <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belize</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Antigua and Barbuda">Antigua and Barbuda</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="Saint Kitts and Nevis">Saint Kitts and Nevis</a> achieved independence from the United Kingdom in the 1980s.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_North_America" title="Geography of North America">Geography of North America</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_South_America" title="Geography of South America">Geography of South America</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Earth-DSCOVR-20150706-IFV.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Earth-DSCOVR-20150706-IFV.jpg/240px-Earth-DSCOVR-20150706-IFV.jpg" decoding="async" width="240" height="236" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Earth-DSCOVR-20150706-IFV.jpg/360px-Earth-DSCOVR-20150706-IFV.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Earth-DSCOVR-20150706-IFV.jpg/480px-Earth-DSCOVR-20150706-IFV.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1788" data-file-height="1756" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Earth-DSCOVR-20150706-IFV.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Satellite photo of the Americas</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Extent">Extent</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Extent">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Americas make up most of the land in Earth's <a href="/wiki/Western_hemisphere" class="mw-redirect" title="Western hemisphere">western hemisphere</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> The northernmost point of the Americas is <a href="/wiki/Kaffeklubben_Island" title="Kaffeklubben Island">Kaffeklubben Island</a>, which is the most northerly point of land on Earth.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> The southernmost point is the islands of <a href="/wiki/Southern_Thule" title="Southern Thule">Southern Thule</a>, although they are sometimes considered part of <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">Antarctica</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> The mainland of the Americas is the world's longest north-to-south landmass. The distance between its two polar extremities, the <a href="/wiki/Boothia_Peninsula" title="Boothia Peninsula">Boothia Peninsula</a> in northern Canada and <a href="/wiki/Cape_Froward" title="Cape Froward">Cape Froward</a> in Chilean <a href="/wiki/Patagonia" title="Patagonia">Patagonia</a>, is roughly 14,000&#160;km (8,700&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-worldbook_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldbook-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> The mainland's most westerly point is the end of the <a href="/wiki/Seward_Peninsula" title="Seward Peninsula">Seward Peninsula</a> in Alaska; <a href="/wiki/Attu_Island" title="Attu Island">Attu Island</a>, further off the Alaskan coast to the west, is considered the westernmost point of the Americas. <a href="/wiki/Ponta_do_Seixas" title="Ponta do Seixas">Ponta do Seixas</a> in northeastern Brazil forms the easternmost extremity of the mainland,<sup id="cite_ref-worldbook_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldbook-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Nordostrundingen" title="Nordostrundingen">Nordostrundingen</a>, in Greenland, is the most easterly point of the continental shelf.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>South America broke off from the west of the <a href="/wiki/Supercontinent" title="Supercontinent">supercontinent</a> <a href="/wiki/Gondwana" title="Gondwana">Gondwana</a> around 135&#160;million years ago, forming its own continent.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Around 15&#160;million years ago, the collision of the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Plate" title="Caribbean Plate">Caribbean Plate</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Plate" title="Pacific Plate">Pacific Plate</a> resulted in the emergence of a series of volcanoes along the border that created a number of islands. The gaps in the archipelago of Central America filled in with material eroded off North America and South America, plus new land created by continued volcanism. By three million years ago, the continents of North America and South America were linked by the <a href="/wiki/Isthmus_of_Panama" title="Isthmus of Panama">Isthmus of Panama</a>, thereby forming the single landmass of the Americas.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Great_American_Interchange" title="Great American Interchange">Great American Interchange</a> resulted in many species being spread across the Americas, such as the <a href="/wiki/Cougar" title="Cougar">cougar</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_World_porcupine" title="New World porcupine">porcupine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Opossum" title="Opossum">opossums</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armadillo" title="Armadillo">armadillos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hummingbird" title="Hummingbird">hummingbirds</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Topography">Topography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Topography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aconcagua_13.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Aconcagua_13.JPG/220px-Aconcagua_13.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Aconcagua_13.JPG/330px-Aconcagua_13.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Aconcagua_13.JPG/440px-Aconcagua_13.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2667" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aconcagua_13.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Aconcagua" title="Aconcagua">Aconcagua</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, is the highest peak in the Americas</div></div></div>
<p>The geography of the western Americas is dominated by the <a href="/wiki/American_cordillera" class="mw-redirect" title="American cordillera">American cordillera</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Andes</a> running along the west coast of South America<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountains" title="Rocky Mountains">Rocky Mountains</a> and other <a href="/wiki/North_American_Cordillera" title="North American Cordillera">North American Cordillera</a> ranges running along the western side of North America.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> The 2,300-kilometer-long (1,400&#160;mi) <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Mountains" title="Appalachian Mountains">Appalachian Mountains</a> run along the east coast of North America from <a href="/wiki/Alabama" title="Alabama">Alabama</a> to <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_(island)" title="Newfoundland (island)">Newfoundland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> North of the Appalachians, the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Cordillera" title="Arctic Cordillera">Arctic Cordillera</a> runs along the eastern coast of Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The largest mountain ranges are the <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Andes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountains" title="Rocky Mountains">Rocky Mountains</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Nevada_(U.S.)" title="Sierra Nevada (U.S.)">Sierra Nevada</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cascade_Range" title="Cascade Range">Cascade Range</a> reach similar altitudes as the <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountains" title="Rocky Mountains">Rocky Mountains</a>, but are significantly smaller. In North America, the greatest number of <a href="/wiki/Fourteener" title="Fourteener">fourteeners</a> are in the United States, and more specifically in the U.S. state of <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">Colorado</a>. The highest peaks of the Americas are located in the <a href="/wiki/List_of_mountains_in_the_Andes" title="List of mountains in the Andes">Andes</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Aconcagua" title="Aconcagua">Aconcagua</a> of <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> being the highest; in North America <a href="/wiki/Denali" title="Denali">Denali</a> (Mount McKinley) in the U.S. state of <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a> is the tallest.
</p><p>Between its coastal mountain ranges, North America has vast flat areas. The <a href="/wiki/Interior_Plains" title="Interior Plains">Interior Plains</a> spread over much of the continent, with low relief.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Shield" title="Canadian Shield">Canadian Shield</a> covers almost 5 million km² of North America and is generally quite flat.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Similarly, the north-east of South America is covered by the flat <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Basin" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon Basin">Amazon Basin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Highlands" title="Brazilian Highlands">Brazilian Highlands</a> on the east coast are fairly smooth but show some variations in landform, while farther south the <a href="/wiki/Gran_Chaco" title="Gran Chaco">Gran Chaco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pampas" title="Pampas">Pampas</a> are broad <a href="/wiki/Lowland" class="mw-redirect" title="Lowland">lowlands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Americas_K%C3%B6ppen_Map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Americas_K%C3%B6ppen_Map.png/240px-Americas_K%C3%B6ppen_Map.png" decoding="async" width="240" height="298" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Americas_K%C3%B6ppen_Map.png/360px-Americas_K%C3%B6ppen_Map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Americas_K%C3%B6ppen_Map.png/480px-Americas_K%C3%B6ppen_Map.png 2x" data-file-width="1096" data-file-height="1360" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Americas_K%C3%B6ppen_Map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Climate zones of the Americas in the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a> system.</div></div></div>
<p>The climate of the Americas varies significantly from region to region. <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest_climate" title="Tropical rainforest climate">Tropical rainforest climate</a> occurs in the latitudes of the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Rainforest" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon Rainforest">Amazon</a>, American <a href="/wiki/Cloud_forest" title="Cloud forest">cloud forests</a>, Florida and <a href="/wiki/Darien_Gap" class="mw-redirect" title="Darien Gap">Darien Gap</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountains" title="Rocky Mountains">Rocky Mountains</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Andes</a>, dry and continental climates are observed. Often the higher altitudes of these mountains are snow-capped.
</p><p>Southeastern North America is well known for its occurrence of <a href="/wiki/Tornadoes" class="mw-redirect" title="Tornadoes">tornadoes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hurricanes" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricanes">hurricanes</a>, of which the vast majority of tornadoes occur in the United States' <a href="/wiki/Tornado_Alley" title="Tornado Alley">Tornado Alley</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Science_News_1_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Science_News_1-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> as well as in the southerly <a href="/wiki/Dixie_Alley" title="Dixie Alley">Dixie Alley</a> in the North American late-winter and early spring seasons. Often parts of the Caribbean are exposed to the violent effects of hurricanes. These weather systems are formed by the collision of dry, cool air from Canada and wet, warm air from the Atlantic.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hydrology">Hydrology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Hydrology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>With coastal mountains and interior plains, the Americas have several large <a href="/wiki/River_basin" class="mw-redirect" title="River basin">river basins</a> that drain the continents. The largest river basin in North America is that of the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi</a>, covering the second largest <a href="/wiki/Drainage_basin" title="Drainage basin">watershed</a> on the planet.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> The Mississippi-Missouri river system drains most of 31 states of the U.S., most of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Plains" title="Great Plains">Great Plains</a>, and large areas between the Rocky and Appalachian mountains. This river is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_rivers_by_length" title="List of rivers by length">fourth longest in the world</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_rivers_by_discharge" title="List of rivers by discharge">tenth most powerful in the world</a>.
</p><p>In North America, to the east of the <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Mountains" title="Appalachian Mountains">Appalachian Mountains</a>, there are no major rivers but rather a series of rivers and streams that flow east with their terminus in the Atlantic Ocean, such as the <a href="/wiki/Hudson_River" title="Hudson River">Hudson River</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_John_River_(Bay_of_Fundy)" title="Saint John River (Bay of Fundy)">Saint John River</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Savannah_River" title="Savannah River">Savannah River</a>. A similar instance arises with central Canadian rivers that drain into <a href="/wiki/Hudson_Bay" title="Hudson Bay">Hudson Bay</a>; the largest being the <a href="/wiki/Churchill_River_(Hudson_Bay)" title="Churchill River (Hudson Bay)">Churchill River</a>. On the west coast of North America, the main rivers are the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_River" title="Colorado River">Colorado River</a>, <a href="/wiki/Columbia_River" title="Columbia River">Columbia River</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yukon_River" title="Yukon River">Yukon River</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fraser_River" title="Fraser River">Fraser River</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sacramento_River" title="Sacramento River">Sacramento River</a>.
</p><p>The Colorado River drains much of the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Rockies" class="mw-redirect" title="Southern Rockies">Southern Rockies</a> and parts of the Great <a href="/wiki/Basin_and_Range_Province" title="Basin and Range Province">Basin and Range Province</a>. The river flows approximately 1,450 miles (2,330&#160;km) into the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_California" title="Gulf of California">Gulf of California</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-largest_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-largest-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> during which over time it has carved out natural phenomena such as the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Canyon" title="Grand Canyon">Grand Canyon</a> and created phenomena such as the <a href="/wiki/Salton_Sea" title="Salton Sea">Salton Sea</a>. The Columbia is a large river, 1,243 miles (2,000&#160;km) long, in central western North America and is the most powerful river on the West Coast of the Americas. In the far northwest of North America, the Yukon drains much of the Alaskan peninsula and flows 1,980 miles (3,190&#160;km)<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> from parts of Yukon and the Northwest Territory to the Pacific. Draining to the Arctic Ocean of Canada, the <a href="/wiki/Mackenzie_River" title="Mackenzie River">Mackenzie River</a> drains waters from the Arctic Great Lakes of Arctic Canada, as opposed to the Saint-Lawrence River that drains the Great Lakes of Southern Canada into the Atlantic Ocean. The Mackenzie River is the largest in Canada and drains 1,805,200 square kilometers (697,000&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The largest river basin in South America is that of the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Basin" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon Basin">Amazon</a>, which has the highest volume flow of any river on Earth.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> The second largest watershed of South America is that of the <a href="/wiki/Paran%C3%A1_River" title="Paraná River">Paraná River</a>, which covers about 2.5 million km².<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecology">Ecology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Ecology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>North America and South America began to develop a shared population of flora and fauna around 2.5 million years ago, when <a href="/wiki/Continental_drift" title="Continental drift">continental drift</a> brought the two continents into contact via the <a href="/wiki/Isthmus_of_Panama" title="Isthmus of Panama">Isthmus of Panama</a>. Initially, the exchange of biota was roughly equal, with North American genera migrating into South America in about the same proportions as South American genera migrated into North America. This exchange is known as the <a href="/wiki/Great_American_Interchange" title="Great American Interchange">Great American Interchange</a>. The exchange became lopsided after roughly a million years, with the total spread of South American genera into North America far more limited in scope than the spread on North American genera into South America.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Countries_and_territories">Countries and territories</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Countries and territories">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_in_the_Americas" title="List of sovereign states and dependent territories in the Americas">List of sovereign states and dependent territories in the Americas</a></div>
<p>There are 35 sovereign states in the Americas, as well as an <a href="/wiki/Danish_Realm" class="mw-redirect" title="Danish Realm">autonomous country</a> of <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a>, three <a href="/wiki/Overseas_department" class="mw-redirect" title="Overseas department">overseas departments</a> of <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, three <a href="/wiki/Overseas_collectivity" title="Overseas collectivity">overseas collectivities</a> of France,<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> and one uninhabited territory of France, eight <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">overseas territories</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, three <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Kingdom of the Netherlands">constituent countries</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, three <a href="/wiki/Public_body_(Netherlands)" title="Public body (Netherlands)">public bodies</a> of the Netherlands, two <a href="/wiki/Territories_of_the_United_States" title="Territories of the United States">unincorporated territories</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, and one uninhabited territory of the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demography">Demography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Demography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_in_the_Americas_by_population" title="List of countries in the Americas by population">List of countries in the Americas by population</a></div>
<p>In 2015 the total population of the Americas was about 985 million people, divided as follows:<sup id="cite_ref-poplistlink_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-poplistlink-81">&#91;note 1&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>North America: 569 million (includes Central America and the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>)</li>
<li>South America: 416 million</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_urban_centers">Largest urban centers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Largest urban centers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Largest_cities_in_the_Americas" title="Largest cities in the Americas">Largest cities in the Americas</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_in_the_Americas_by_population" class="mw-redirect" title="List of metropolitan areas in the Americas by population">List of metropolitan areas in the Americas by population</a></div>
<p>There are three urban centers that each hold titles for being the largest population area based on the three main demographic concepts:<sup id="cite_ref-wider_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wider-104">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/City_proper" title="City proper">City proper</a></li></ul>
<dl><dd>A city proper is the locality with legally fixed boundaries and an administratively recognized urban status that is usually characterized by some form of local government.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup></dd></dl>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Urban_area" title="Urban area">Urban area</a></li></ul>
<dl><dd>An urban area is characterized by higher population density and vast human features in comparison to areas surrounding it. Urban areas may be cities, towns or conurbations, but the term is not commonly extended to rural settlements such as villages and hamlets. Urban areas are created and further developed by the process of urbanization and do not include large swaths of rural land, as do metropolitan areas.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></dd></dl>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_area" title="Metropolitan area">Metropolitan area</a></li></ul>
<dl><dd>Unlike an urban area, a metropolitan area includes not only the urban area, but also satellite cities <i>plus intervening rural land</i> that is socio-economically connected to the urban core city, typically by employment ties through commuting, with the urban core city being the primary labor market.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></dd></dl>
<p>In accordance with these definitions, the three largest population centers in the Americas are: <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a>, anchor to the largest metropolitan area in the Americas; New York City, anchor to the largest urban area in the Americas; and São Paulo, the largest city proper in the Americas. All three cities maintain <a href="/wiki/Global_city#Alpha" title="Global city">Alpha</a> classification and large scale influence.
</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional center">
	<li class="gallerycaption">Urban centers within the Americas</li>
