<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnology">Ethnology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Ethnology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">June 2014</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The population of the Americas is made up of the descendants of four large <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">ethnic groups</a> and their combinations.
</p>
<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">Indigenous peoples of the Americas</a>, being <a href="/wiki/Amerindian" class="mw-redirect" title="Amerindian">Amerindians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Inuit" title="Inuit">Inuit</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Aleut_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Aleut people">Aleuts</a>.</li>
<li>Those of European ancestry, mainly Spanish, British and Irish, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">German</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italians" title="Italians">Italian</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_people" title="French people">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polish_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Polish people">Polish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_(ethnic_group)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dutch (ethnic group)">Dutch</a>, Russians and <a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">Scandinavians</a>.</li>
<li>Those of <a href="/wiki/Afro-American_peoples_of_the_Americas" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-American peoples of the Americas">African</a> ancestry, mainly of West African descent.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Asian_people" title="Asian people">Asians</a>, that is, those of <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Asia" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Asia">Eastern</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asian</a> ancestry.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">Mestizos</a> (<a href="/wiki/Metis_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Metis people">Metis people</a> in Canada), those of mixed European and Amerindian ancestry.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mulatto" title="Mulatto">Mulattoes</a>, people of mixed African and European ancestry.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Zambo" title="Zambo">Zambos</a> (Spanish) or <a href="/wiki/Cafuzo" class="mw-redirect" title="Cafuzo">Cafuzos</a> (Portuguese), those of mixed African and Amerindian ancestry.</li></ul>
<p>The majority of the population live in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>, named for its predominant cultures, rooted in <a href="/wiki/Romance-speaking_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Romance-speaking Europe">Latin Europe</a> (including the two dominant languages, Spanish and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>, both <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">Romance languages</a>), more specifically in the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian</a> nations of <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> and Spain (hence the use of the term <a href="/wiki/Ibero-America" title="Ibero-America">Ibero-America</a> as a synonym). Latin America is typically contrasted with <a href="/wiki/Anglo-America" title="Anglo-America">Anglo-America</a>, where English, a <a href="/wiki/Germanic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Germanic language">Germanic language</a>, is prevalent, and which comprises Canada (with the exception of <a href="/wiki/Canadian_French" title="Canadian French">francophone Canada</a> rooted in Latin Europe [France]—see <a href="/wiki/Qu%C3%A9bec" class="mw-redirect" title="Québec">Québec</a> and <a href="/wiki/Acadia" title="Acadia">Acadia</a>) and the United States. Both countries are located in North America, with cultures deriving predominantly from <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxon" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo-Saxon">Anglo-Saxon</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic</a> roots.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Latin_America" title="Religion in Latin America">Religion in Latin America</a>, <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_North_America" title="Religion in North America">Religion in North America</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_the_Americas" class="mw-redirect" title="Christianity in the Americas">Christianity in the Americas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_the_Americas" title="Islam in the Americas">Islam in the Americas</a></div>
<p>The most prevalent faiths in the Americas are as follows:
</p>
<ul><li>Christianity (86 percent)<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
<ul><li>Roman Catholicism: Practiced by 69 percent<sup id="cite_ref-pewlat_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pewlat-119">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> of the Latin American population, 81 percent<sup id="cite_ref-pewlat_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pewlat-119">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> in Mexico and 61 percent<sup id="cite_ref-pewlat_119-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pewlat-119">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> in Brazil whose Roman Catholic population of 123 million is the greatest of any nation's; approximately 24 percent of the United States' population<sup id="cite_ref-CIAWFB_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIAWFB-120">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> and about 39 percent of Canada's.<sup id="cite_ref-religion2011d_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-religion2011d-121">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Protestantism: Practiced mostly in the United States, where half of the population are Protestant, Canada, with slightly more than a quarter of the population, and Greenland; there is a growing contingent of <a href="/wiki/Evangelicalism" title="Evangelicalism">Evangelical</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pentecostal" class="mw-redirect" title="Pentecostal">Pentecostal</a> movements in predominantly Catholic Latin America.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodoxy</a>: Found mostly in the United States (1 percent) and Canada; this Christian group is growing faster than many other Christian groups in Canada and now represents roughly 3 percent of the Canadian population.<sup id="cite_ref-religion2011d_121-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-religion2011d-121">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Non-denominational_Christianity" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-denominational Christianity">Non-denominational Christians</a> and other Christians (some 1,000 different Christian denominations and sects practiced in the Americas).</li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Irreligion" title="Irreligion">Irreligion</a>: About 12 percent, including atheists and agnostics, as well as those who profess some form of spirituality but do not identify themselves as members of any organized religion.</li>
<li>Islam: Together, Muslims constitute about 1 percent of the North American population and 0.3 percent of all Latin Americans. It is practiced by 3 percent <sup id="cite_ref-religion2011d_121-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-religion2011d-121">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> of Canadians and 0.6 percent of the U.S. population.<sup id="cite_ref-CIAWFB_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIAWFB-120">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> has the largest Muslim population in Latin America with up to 600,000 persons, or 1.9 percent of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-stateirf_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stateirf-123">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Judaism (practiced by 2 percent of North Americans—approximately 2.5 percent of the U.S. population and 1.2 percent of Canadians<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>—and 0.23 percent of Latin Americans—Argentina has the largest Jewish population in Latin America with 200,000 members)<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Other faiths include <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>; <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>; <a href="/wiki/Sikhism" title="Sikhism">Sikhism</a>; <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="Bahá&#39;í Faith">Bahá'í Faith</a>; a wide variety of indigenous religions, many of which can be categorized as <a href="/wiki/Animist" class="mw-redirect" title="Animist">animistic</a>; <a href="/wiki/New_age" class="mw-redirect" title="New age">new age</a> religions and many <a href="/wiki/African_traditional_religion" class="mw-redirect" title="African traditional religion">African</a> and African-derived religions. <a href="/wiki/Syncretism" title="Syncretism">Syncretic</a> faiths can also be found throughout the Americas.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_languages_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous languages of the Americas">Indigenous languages of the Americas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_North_America" title="Languages of North America">Languages of North America</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_South_America" title="Languages of South America">Languages of South America</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Languages_of_the_American_Continent.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Languages_of_the_American_Continent.png/220px-Languages_of_the_American_Continent.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="244" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Languages_of_the_American_Continent.png/330px-Languages_of_the_American_Continent.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Languages_of_the_American_Continent.png/440px-Languages_of_the_American_Continent.png 2x" data-file-width="624" data-file-height="691" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Languages_of_the_American_Continent.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Languages spoken in the Americas</div></div></div>
<p>Various <a href="/wiki/Language" title="Language">languages</a> are spoken in the Americas. Some are of European origin, others are spoken by indigenous peoples or are the mixture of various languages like the different creoles.<sup id="cite_ref-latbar_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latbar-130">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The most widely spoken language in the Americas is <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> The dominant language of <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a> is Spanish, though the most populous nation in Latin America, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, speaks <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>. Small enclaves of <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>-, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>- and <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>-speaking regions also exist in Latin America, notably in <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belize</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a> respectively. <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Creole" title="Haitian Creole">Haitian Creole</a> is dominant in the nation of <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>, where French is also spoken. <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_languages_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous languages of the Americas">Native languages</a> are more prominent in Latin America than in <a href="/wiki/Anglo-America" title="Anglo-America">Anglo-America</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Nahuatl_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Nahuatl language">Nahuatl</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quechua_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Quechua languages">Quechua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aymara_language" title="Aymara language">Aymara</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guaran%C3%AD_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Guaraní language">Guaraní</a> as the most common. Various other native languages are spoken with less frequency across both Anglo-America and Latin America. <a href="/wiki/Creole_language" title="Creole language">Creole languages</a> other than Haitian Creole are also spoken in parts of Latin America.
</p><p>The dominant language of Anglo-America is English. French is also official in <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, where it is the predominant language in <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a> and an official language in <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">New Brunswick</a> along with English. It is also an important language in <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a>, and in parts of <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire" title="New Hampshire">New Hampshire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maine" title="Maine">Maine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vermont" title="Vermont">Vermont</a>. Spanish has kept an ongoing presence in the <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_United_States" title="Southwestern United States">Southwestern United States</a>, which formed part of the <a href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_New_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Viceroyalty of New Spain">Viceroyalty of New Spain</a>, especially in <a href="/wiki/Californio" title="Californio">California</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a>, where <a href="/wiki/New_Mexican_Spanish" title="New Mexican Spanish">a distinct variety of Spanish</a> spoken since the 17th century has survived. It has more recently become widely spoken in other parts of the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> because of heavy immigration from Latin America. High levels of immigration in general have brought great linguistic diversity to Anglo-America, with over 300 languages known to be spoken in the United States alone, but most languages are spoken only in small enclaves and by relatively small immigrant groups.
</p><p>The nations of Guyana, Suriname, and Belize are generally considered<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (July 2012)">by whom?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> not to fall into either Anglo-America or Latin America because of their language differences from Latin America, geographic differences from Anglo-America, and cultural and historical differences from both regions; English is the primary language of Guyana and Belize, and Dutch is the primary language of Suriname.
</p><p>Most of the non-native languages have, to different degrees, evolved differently from the mother country, but are usually still mutually intelligible. Some have combined, however, which has even resulted in completely new languages, such as <a href="/wiki/Papiamento" title="Papiamento">Papiamento</a>, which is a combination of Portuguese, Spanish, Dutch (representing the respective colonizers), native <a href="/wiki/Arawak_peoples" class="mw-redirect" title="Arawak peoples">Arawak</a>, various <a href="/wiki/African_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="African languages">African languages</a>, and, more recently English. The <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a> <a href="/wiki/Portu%C3%B1ol" title="Portuñol">Portuñol</a>, a mixture of Portuguese and Spanish, is spoken in the border regions of Brazil and neighboring Spanish-speaking countries.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> More specifically, <a href="/wiki/Riverense_Portu%C3%B1ol_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Riverense Portuñol language">Riverense Portuñol</a> is spoken by around 100,000 people in the border regions of Brazil and <a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">Uruguay</a>. Because of <a href="/wiki/Immigration" title="Immigration">immigration</a>, there are many communities where other languages are spoken from all parts of the world, especially in the United States, Brazil, <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, Canada, <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">Costa Rica</a> and Uruguay—very important destinations for immigrants.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="English">English</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: English">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/American_(word)" title="American (word)">American (word)</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">Speakers of English</a> generally refer to the <a href="/wiki/Landmass" title="Landmass">landmasses</a> of North America and South America as <i>the Americas</i>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">Western Hemisphere</a></i>, or the <i><a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> The adjective <i>American</i> may be used to indicate something pertains to the Americas,<sup id="cite_ref-OEDAMERICAN_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OEDAMERICAN-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> but this term is primarily used in English to indicate something pertaining to the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-OEDAMERICAN_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OEDAMERICAN-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-oxfcdn_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oxfcdn-149">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> Some non-ambiguous alternatives exist, such as the adjective <i>Pan-American</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> or <i>New Worlder</i> as a demonym for a resident of the closely related <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-OED&#124;New_Worlder_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OED|New_Worlder-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Use of <i>America</i> in the hemispherical sense is sometimes retained, or can occur when translated from other languages.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> For example, the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_National_Olympic_Committees" title="Association of National Olympic Committees">Association of National Olympic Committees</a> (ANOC) in Paris maintains a single continental association for "America", represented by one of the five <a href="/wiki/Olympic_rings" class="mw-redirect" title="Olympic rings">Olympic rings</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>American linguist <a href="/wiki/H.L._Mencken" class="mw-redirect" title="H.L. Mencken">H.L. Mencken</a> said, " The Latin-Americans use Norteamericano in formal writing, but, save in Panama, prefer nicknames in colloquial speech."<sup id="cite_ref-Mencken_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mencken-153">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> To avoid "American" one can use constructed terms in their languages derived from "United States" or even "North America".<sup id="cite_ref-oxfcdn_149-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oxfcdn-149">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> In Canada, its southern neighbor is often referred to as "the United States", "the U.S.A.", or (informally) "the States", while U.S. citizens are generally referred to as "Americans".<sup id="cite_ref-oxfcdn_149-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oxfcdn-149">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> Most Canadians resent being referred to as "Americans".<sup id="cite_ref-oxfcdn_149-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oxfcdn-149">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish">Spanish</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Spanish">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Spanish, <i>América</i> is a single continent composed of the <a href="/wiki/Subcontinent" class="mw-redirect" title="Subcontinent">subcontinents</a> of <i>América del Sur</i> and <i>América del Norte</i>, the <a href="/wiki/Land_bridge" title="Land bridge">land bridge</a> of <i>América Central</i>, and the islands of the <i><a href="/wiki/Antilles" title="Antilles">Antillas</a></i>. <i>Americano</i> or <i>americana</i> in Spanish refers to a person from <i>América</i> in a similar way that <i>europeo</i> or <i>europea</i> refers to a person from <i>Europa</i>. The terms <i>sudamericano/a</i>, <i>centroamericano/a</i>, <i>antillano/a</i> and <i>norteamericano/a</i> can be used to more specifically refer to the location where a person may live.
</p><p>Citizens of the United States of America are normally referred to by the term <i>estadounidense</i> (rough literal translation: "<a href="/wiki/United_Statesian" class="mw-redirect" title="United Statesian">United Statesian</a>") instead of <i>americano</i> or <i>americana</i> which is discouraged,<sup id="cite_ref-norteamerica_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-norteamerica-156">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-estadosunidos_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-estadosunidos-157">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> and the country's name itself is officially translated as <i>Estados Unidos de América</i> (United States of America), commonly abbreviated as <i>Estados Unidos</i> (EEUU).<sup id="cite_ref-estadosunidos_157-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-estadosunidos-157">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> Also, the term <i>norteamericano</i> (North American) may refer to a citizen of the United States. This term is primarily used to refer to citizens of the United States, and less commonly to those of other North American countries.<sup id="cite_ref-norteamerica_156-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-norteamerica-156">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Portuguese">Portuguese</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Portuguese">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Portuguese, <i><a href="https://pt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Am%C3%A9rica" class="extiw" title="pt:América">América</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-AmericaPortBE_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AmericaPortBE-158">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> is a single continent composed of <i>América do Sul</i> (South America), <i>América Central</i> (Central America) and <i>América do Norte</i> (North America).<sup id="cite_ref-AmericaME_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AmericaME-159">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> It can be ambiguous, as <i>América</i> can be used to refer to the United States of America, but is avoided in print and formal environments.<sup id="cite_ref-EstadosUnidosIt_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EstadosUnidosIt-160">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EstadosUnidosESPN_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EstadosUnidosESPN-161">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="French">French</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: French">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In French the word <i>américain</i> may be used for things relating to the Americas; however, similar to English, it is most often used for things relating to the United States, with the term <i>états-unien</i> sometimes used for clarity. <i>Panaméricain</i> may be used as an adjective to refer to the Americas without ambiguity.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> French speakers may use the noun <i>Amérique</i> to refer to the whole landmass as one continent, or two continents, <i>Amérique du Nord</i> and <i>Amérique du Sud</i>. In French, <i>Amérique</i> is seldom used to refer to the United States, leading to some ambiguity when it is. Similar to English usage, <i>les Amériques</i> or <i>des Amériques</i> is used to refer unambiguously to the Americas.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dutch">Dutch</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Dutch">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Dutch, the word <i>Amerika</i> mostly refers to the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> Although the United States is equally often referred to as <i>de Verenigde Staten</i> ("the United States") or <i>de VS</i> ("the US"), <i>Amerika</i> relatively rarely refers to the Americas, but it is the only commonly used Dutch word for the Americas. This often leads to ambiguity; and to stress that something concerns the Americas as a whole, Dutch uses a combination, namely <i>Noord- en Zuid-Amerika</i> (North and South America).
</p><p>Latin America is generally referred to as <i>Latijns Amerika</i> or <i>Midden-Amerika</i> for Central America.
</p><p>The adjective <i>Amerikaans</i> is most often used for things or people relating to the United States. There are no alternative words to distinguish between things relating to the United States or to the Americas. Dutch uses the local alternative for things relating to elsewhere in the Americas, such as <i>Argentijns</i> for <a href="/wiki/Argentine_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Argentine people">Argentine</a>, etc.
</p>

<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">Dominica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a> have the fastest-growing economy in the Americas according to the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> (IMF),<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2016, five to seven countries in the southern part of the Americas had weakening economies in decline, compared to only three countries in the northern part of the Americas.<sup id="cite_ref-IMFNorthAmericaGDP_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMFNorthAmericaGDP-167">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IMFUNASURGDP_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMFUNASURGDP-168">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> Haiti has the lowest GDP per capita in the Americas, although its economy was growing slightly as of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Americas&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-IMFNorthAmericaGDP_167-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMFNorthAmericaGDP-167">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IMFUNASURGDP_168-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMFUNASURGDP-168">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-poplistlink-81"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-poplistlink_81-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-poplistlink_81-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">See <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_population" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries by population">List of countries by population</a> for references.</span>

<li id="cite_note-103"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-103">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Includes the states of Hawaii and Alaska, which are both separated from the <a href="/wiki/Contiguous_United_States" title="Contiguous United States">US mainland</a>, with Hawaii distant from the North American landmass in the Pacific Ocean and therefore more commonly associated with the other territories of Oceania, while Alaska is located between <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> and <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a> (<a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>).</span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-18"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-18">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Marjorie Fee and Janice MacAlpine, <i>Oxford Guide to Canadian English Usage</i> (2008) page 36 says "In Canada, <i>American</i> is used almost exclusively in reference to the United States and its citizens." Others, including <i>The New Zealand Oxford Dictionary</i>, <i>The Canadian Oxford Dictionary</i>, <i>The Australian Oxford Dictionary</i> and <i>The Concise Oxford English Dictionary</i> all specify both the Americas and the United States in their definition of "American".</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-oxfordc-19"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-oxfordc_19-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-oxfordc_19-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">"America." <i>The Oxford Companion to the English Language</i> (<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/><a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-19-214183-X" title="Special:BookSources/0-19-214183-X">0-19-214183-X</a>). McArthur, Tom, ed., 1992. New York: Oxford University Press, p. 33: "[16c: from the feminine of <i>Americus</i>, the Latinized first name of the explorer Amerigo Vespucci (1454–1512). The name <i>America</i> first appeared on a map in 1507 by the German cartographer Martin Waldseemüller, referring to the area now called Brazil]. Since the 16c, a name of the western hemisphere, often in the plural <i>Americas</i> and more or less synonymous with <i>the New World</i>. Since the 18c, a name of the United States of America. The second sense is now primary in English:&#160;... However, the term is open to uncertainties:&#160;..."</span>
</li>
